Switch Online was already not a good deal, but the Expansion Pack was where I drew the line. I didn’t buy it, and the more videos and articles I watched the more I’m glad that I didn’t buy it, because from what I could tell everything fans had been doing for decades was better than what Nintendo was offering in the present day. \n\nThe Expansion Pack gives you the ability to play nine Nintendo 64 games and 14 Sega Mega Drive games. There’s one big problem however: the emulation. The N64 and Mega Drive games have not been natively ported and instead have been emulated using a Nintendo-developed emulator. Now there’s nothing wrong with emulation, but the problem is that the emulation on the Expansion Pack is horrible. In Ocarina of Time, the reflection of Link in the water before the Dark Link fight was impressive at the time; combined with the fog gave an unsettling, mysterious vibe to the scene. The Switch Online emulator on the other hand completely removes the fog from the Dark Link fight, killing the atmosphere and making it look dull.\nHere's an image for reference:\n[img[zelda]]
The Nintendo Switch Online membership is currently the only way to play online for most first-party games, with only about a dozen of third-party games not requiring the membership, so it’s very important for the Nintendo Switch. Because of that many people assume that it’s a good deal, when in reality it’s just an okay deal.\n\n[[Next|Quality]]
Switch Online Review
Imsad2
Let’s start with the actual quality of the deal. As the name suggests, it lets you play online, but the actual online part of it is only partially good. I’ve never really had problems with my ping, but many have and have complained about it to Nintendo. Nintendo seems to wear mufflers on their ears however and don’t seem to really care about the complaints, similar to their response to Joy-Con Drift. \n\n \n\nThis is a big problem with Nintendo; they attack fans over the quality of netplay on emulators, but barely do anything to improve their own services. \n\n[[Next|In-game rewards]]\n
The mobile app is the dumbest part of the membership by far mainly because, you guessed it, it’s nothing but pointless junk. OK ok, I’ll give Nintendo the benefit of the doubt here. It is quite a nice novelty…if it was actually useful. \n\n \n\nThe app has three different sections dedicated to different games; Smash World for Smash Bros., SplatNet for Splatoon 2 and NookLink for Animal Crossing: New Horizons. There’s also voice chat for only a dozen games, which is completely negated by the fact that you can use pretty much any video call software to do exactly that. \n\n \n\nYou can do what Smash World does on YouTube. You can do what SplatNet does in the actual game. And NookLink…NookLink is kinda useless. I mean, you can scan designs, but you can do that in-game. You can chat with people, but you can already do that with an app on the NookPhone. And finally, you can check on your friends if they’re online. You can already do that in the game. I SMELL POINTLESS! \n\n[[Next|Expansion Pack]]
The in-game rewards are quite possibly the most pointless parts of Switch Online. They give you free stuff for games that use the service, but only for a dozen games; I’ll be looking at the rewards for Splatoon 2, Super Smash Bros. Ultimate and Animal Crossing: New Horizons. \n\n \n\nFirst, let’s look at the rewards for Splatoon 2. The Splatoon series’s most prominent feature is online gameplay, and for Splatoon 2’s online gameplay a Switch Online subscription is required for use. So, not only do you have to pay £40 for the game, but you’re also charged £20 a month just to have a bit of fun with your friends. It’s already not a great deal, and the reward just adds salt to the wound. \n\n \n\nSplatoon 2’s reward are special shirts exclusively for Switch Online members, presumably to “show off” to people during play. But here’s the thing; for people to see you wearing the shirt, you need to play online, but the only way to play online in Splatoon 2 is to have the membership…I smell pointless! \n\n \n\nSuper Smash Bros. Ultimate’s in-game reward for purchasing the membership is just a couple of SP and a free Spirit…again, I smell pointless! \n\n \n\nAnimal Crossing: New Horizons’s in-game reward is a Nintendo Switch Lite. Not a real one, obviously, but an in-game item that would otherwise cost 19,980 bells(the game’s currency) at the Nook Stop. This one isn’t as dumb as the other ones, but it’s still quite boring mainly because: it does nothing at all! Crazy innit?\n[[Next|Mobile app]]
